[FONT 0][SPACING 1][ALIGN 2][COLOR 3]Before the Mystery Gift is Sent
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The game will be saved after you read through these\ninstructions--Mystery Gift distribution will start then.\nMake sure you've already obtained the Pokédex in the\nDS Pokémon game you will communicate with.\n(Do not turn the DS system's power on yet.)
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Distribution will only be active for\n[COLOR 3]3 minutes[COLOR 5] (180 seconds).\nIf you can't receive the gift within 3 minutes,\neven if it's due to a problem with the DS system,\nyour Poké Coupons will not be refunded.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Mystery Gift is distributed using a [COLOR 3]Wonder Card[COLOR 5].\nIf your DS Pokémon game already has 3 Wonder Cards,\nthe game will not be able to receive any more.\nDelete a Wonder Card so that you have no more than\n2 Wonder Cards, and then start distribution.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Also, a DS Pokémon game can receive only one of\neach kind of gift.\nIf the DS Pokémon game already received the gift\nthat you are trying to distribute now, the Game Card\nwill not be able to receive it again.

[FONT 0][SPACING 1][ALIGN 2]Mystery Gift Distribution
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]You are now ready to begin Mystery Gift distribution!\nMake sure your DS Pokémon game is ready.\n(Do not turn on the power yet.)\nDistribution will only be active for\n[COLOR 3]3 minutes[COLOR 5] (180 seconds).\nFollow the instructions on the screen.
[FONT 0][SPACING 1][ALIGN 2]Start Distribution

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When a Pokémon loses all of its HP during\nbattle, it faints and is no longer able\nto battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]You will win a battle if you defeat all of your\nopponent's Pokémon and make them faint.\nOn the other hand, you will lose if all of\nyour Pokémon faint.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are two styles of Pokémon battles:\nSingle Battle and Double Battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Single Battle is where you and your\nopponent each send out one Pokémon\nto fight.\nA Double Battle is where you and your\nopponent each send out two Pokémon\nto fight.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Both the Single and Double Battles\nare available in the Colosseum Mode.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the DS Battle Mode, you can play\na Mix Battle.\nA Mix Battle is where you exchange one\nPokémon with your opponent and then\nbattle it out.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Pokémon battles use a turn-based system,\nmeaning that both you and your opponent\ntake a turn giving a command. Once each\nside finishes its action (such as using a\nmove or switching Pokémon) the turn ends.\nThis is repeated until someone wins.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are two Level Rules in\na Colosseum Battle:\n["Lv."] 30 Open and ["Lv."] 50 All.\n \nPokémon of any level can enter\na battle using either of the rules.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In ["Lv."] 30 Open, the level of the opponent's\nPokémon are set to the same level as the\nhighest-level Pokémon on your Battle Pass.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, in a Single Battle, if the\nPokémon on your Battle Pass are\n["Lv."] 1, ["Lv."] 5, ["Lv."] 40, ["Lv."] 80, ["Lv."] 8,\nand ["Lv."] 2, the levels of all of the\nopponent's Pokémon will be ["Lv."] 80.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, in ["Lv."] 30 Open, the lowest-level \nPokémon that the opponent has will\nbe ["Lv."] 30. Therefore, even if you have\nPokémon on your Battle Pass that are lower\nthan ["Lv."] 30, your opponent's Pokémon will\nall be ["Lv."] 30.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In ["Lv."] 50 All, all Pokémon participating in\nthe battle (regardless of their real levels)\nwill be ["Lv."] 50.\nHowever, the moves a Pokémon can use\nin battle remain the same as they would\nat their original level.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If you have Pokémon on your Battle Pass\nthat are higher than ["Lv."] 50, their levels will\nall be lowered to ["Lv."] 50.\nIf you have any Pokémon that are lower than\n["Lv."] 50, their levels will be raised to ["Lv."] 50.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]At the start of each turn, three command\noptions will be displayed on the screen.\nThese commands are FIGHT, POKéMON,\nand GIVE IN.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose FIGHT to use one of your Pokémon's\nmoves, choose POKéMON when you want to\ncheck a Pokémon's info or switch out your\ncurrent Pokémon with another from your\nparty, and choose GIVE IN to quit\nthe battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]On the upper part of the screen is the\nstatus panel which shows the Pokémon's HP\nand any current status problems they have.\nThe blue panel on the left is your Pokémon,\nand the red panel on the right is your\nopponent's Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose FIGHT when you want to use\na Pokémon's move during the battle.\nAll of the Pokémon's moves are displayed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]After selecting a move, choose which\nPokémon you want to use the move on.\nThe red panels show the opponent's\nPokémon, while the blue panels show\nyour Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Your command will be complete once you\nchoose which Pokémon you want to use\nthe move on.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose the POKéMON command when your\nPokémon in battle are getting beat down,\nor if you want to shift in a Pokémon that\nmight have an advantageous matchup\nagainst the opponent's Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]After you select the POKéMON command,\nthe other Pokémon in your party will\nbe displayed. Choose the Pokémon you want\nto send into battle.\nAfter that, another three command buttons\nwill be displayed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose the Shift command to send the\nselected Pokémon into battle.\nThe Pokémon Skills command enables you\nto check the selected Pokémon's stats.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose Moves to see the moves of\nthe selected Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose the GIVE IN command to quit\nthe battle.\nHowever, this will be counted as a loss,\nand you'll be taken back to the receptionist.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Each Pokémon is able to hold one item.\nThere is a chance that a Pokémon in battle\nwill use the item on its own.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Trainer can't use items in this game.\nIt's best to have your Pokémon hold an\nitem that you want them to use in battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Each Pokémon has its own unique stats.\nThere are six kinds of stats. These are HP,\nAttack, Defense, Special Attack, Special\nDefense, and Speed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Stats can affect the Pokémon's actions\nwhile in battle, and might even affect the\noutcome of the battle. 
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Hit Points (HP) are what measure\na Pokémon's health.\nIf your Pokémon's HP hit zero, the Pokémon\nfaints and will no longer be able to fight.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Since a Trainer can't use items in this game,\nhave your Pokémon hold an item or use\na move to recover HP.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Attack and Defense stats determine\nthe effectiveness of physical moves;\nthe higher the Attack stat is, the more\ndamage a physical move causes.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]On the other hand, a higher Defense stat\nreduces the amount of damage a physical\nmove can deal when you are hit by it.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Special Attack and Special Defense\nstats determine the effectiveness of\nspecial moves; the higher the Special\nAttack is, the more damage a special move\ncauses.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]On the other hand, a higher Special Defense\nstat reduces the amount of damage\na special move can deal when you are\nhit by it.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Speed stat determines who will attack\nfirst once commands have been given.\nThe higher the Speed stat is, the quicker\na Pokémon will use their move.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are also some moves, such as Quick\nAttack or Shadow Sneak, which enable\na Pokémon to attack first, regardless\nof its Speed stat.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Pokémon holding the Quick Claw item\ncan sometimes attack first, even if it\nis normally a little bit slow.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Pokémon are categorized into 17 different\ntypes.\nFor example, TURTWIG is a Grass type,\nCHIMCHAR is a Fire type, and PIPLUP is\na Water type.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Some Pokémon have two different types.\nThese are called dual-type Pokémon.\nThe amount of damage they will take from\nan opponent's move will differ depending\non your Pokémon's two types.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Similar to Pokémon types, moves are\nalso categorized into 17 different types.\nFor example, Razor Leaf is a Grass-type\nmove, Ember is a Fire-type move, and Bubble\nis a Water-type move.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are no moves that are dual type;\nmoves are always categorized as one type.\nHow much damage your attack does to an\nopponent differs based on the move's type.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are matchup advantages between\na Pokémon's type and the move type being\nused on it. For example, Grass-type moves\nhave an advantageous matchup against\nWater-type Pokémon. The Grass-type move\nwill cause twice the normal damage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, Grass-type moves have a\ndisadvantageous matchup against\nFire-type Pokémon. The Grass-type move\nwill only cause half the normal amount\nof damage. 
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are various kinds of moves.\nSome cause damage to the opponent's\nPokémon, while others affect a Pokémon's\nstatus, or change the stats of your or your\nopponent's Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Pokémon can know up to four moves\nat once. What kinds of moves you have\nyour Pokémon learn is one of the key\nfactors that will affect how well they do\nin a battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Pay close attention to the power and\naccuracy rating of a move before you have\nyour Pokémon learn it.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Any move that can deal damage to an\nopponent's Pokémon will have a power\nrating. The higher the power rating is,\nthe more damage that move can cause.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Also, the accuracy rating of a move varies\ndepending on the move. The higher a move's\naccuracy rating is, the easier it is to hit the\nopponent's Pokémon. The lower a move's\naccuracy rating is, the more likely it will be\nto miss.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves are divided into three categories:\nphysical, special, and status.\nPhysical and special moves are used to\ndeal direct damage to the opponent's\nPokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Status moves are used to affect the\ncurrent status or stats of your or your\nopponent's Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The damage a physical move causes is\ndetermined by the Attack stat of the\nPokémon using it, as well as the Defense\nstat of the Pokémon on the receiving end\nof the move.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If a Pokémon has a high Attack stat and\nuses a physical move, it will cause more\ndamage. On the other hand, when a Pokémon\nwith a high Defense stat gets attacked by\na physical move, they will take less damage. 
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The damage a special move causes is\ndetermined by the Special Attack stat of\nthe Pokémon using it, as well as the Special\nDefense stat of the Pokémon on the\nreceiving end of the move.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If a Pokémon has a high Special Attack\nstat and uses a special move, it will cause\nmore damage.\nAlso, a Pokémon that has a high Special\nDefense stat and is attacked by a special\nmove will take less damage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves that can alter a Pokémon's status\nor stats are called status moves. There are\nmany kinds of status moves.\nSome of them cause status problems, such\nas sleep or poison, while others raise or\nlower stats and can even restore lost HP.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Make good use of these moves and you'll\nfind that you have an advantage in battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A status problem is when a Pokémon's status\nis negatively affected during battle.\nSome status problems are poison, paralysis,\nfrozen, burn, sleep, and confusion.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If a Pokémon is suffering from a status\nproblem, it is likely to be at a huge\ndisadvantage in battle. It may not be able\nto make any moves, or it can even lose\nHP over time.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Some status problems are cured after\na certain number of turns. However, there\nare also others that can't be cured without\nthe help of certain moves or items.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Trainer can't use items in this game,\nso it's a good idea to make sure to have\nyour Pokémon hold an item or learn a move\nthat can cure status problems.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]What Are Pokémon Abilities?
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]What Do Abilities Do?
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Pokémon Held Items
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Item Effects
[FONT 0][SPACING 0]Type and Move Matchups
[FONT 0][SPACING 0]Critical Hits
[FONT 0][SPACING 0]Dual-Type Pokémon
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Move-Damage Multipliers
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Hitting Multiple Opponents
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Moves with Additional Effects
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Move Order
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Direct-Attack Moves
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Moves That Affect All: 1
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Moves That Affect All: 2
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Recovering from Status Problems
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Adding Additional Effects
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Abilities and Status Problems
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Choosing Pokémon
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Effectively Switching Pokémon
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Protecting Your Weaknesses with Moves
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Checking Pokémon Stats
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Move Combinations
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Physical- and Special-Attack Categories
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Order of Action in Double Battle
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Ability-Effect Timing
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Moves with Changed Effects
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Changed Ability Effects
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Each Pokémon has an ability.              \nWhen a battle begins, this ability starts\nto take effect without any player input.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are various kinds of abilities.\nDepending on the ability, different effects\nare exhibited. Certain types of moves won't\nhave any effect, or a Pokémon won't become \nafflicted with specific status problems.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Each Pokémon species has a different\nability. Even similar Pokémon of the\nsame species will sometimes have\ndifferent abilities.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, Ground-type moves won't\nhave any effect against a Pokémon that\nhas Levitate as an ability.\nWhen a direct attack is used against\na Pokémon that has Static as an ability,\nthe attacker may become paralyzed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Pokémon that have the ability\nWater Absorb restore HP when\nattacked by a Water-type move.\nThus it's important to think about the\nability an opponent's Pokémon might\nhave.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Pokémon can hold only one item.\nSome items disappear once used, while\nother items can be used repeatedly.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if a Pokémon holds a\nLum Berry, it will use it immediately once \nit has suffered any status problem during\nbattle. However, the Berry will disappear\nonce used.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]On the other hand, the held item \nLeftovers will restore a holder's HP\nlittle by little each turn and it won't\ndisappear.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are many types of items:\n・Items that raise a certain \n  move type's power\n・Items that raise a Pokémon's stats,\n  such as Speed or Special Attack\n・Items that heal HP or status problems
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Have a Pokémon hold an item that will\nbe used effectively in a battle.\nRemember to consider a Pokémon's stats,\nits type, and the moves it knows.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If a Pokémon uses the same move type\nas its own type, the usual damage \ncaused to the opponent will be\n1.5 times larger.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if the Grass-type TURTWIG\nuses the Grass-type move Razor Leaf,\nthe attack will be stronger than usual.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]With a critical hit, the usual damage\nwill be twice as large. There are many \nmoves, such as Slash or Cross Chop,\nthat have an increased chance\nof a critical hit.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are also held items that will \nboost a holder's chance of a critical hit.\nThe Scope Lens is one such item.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Dual-type Pokémon make matchups\na bit more complex. There is a chance \nthat if a type has a disadvantage against\na move, its other type will balance out\nthis disadvantage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]On the other hand, there are cases\nwhere being a dual type may increase\na Pokémon's disadvantage against \nmoves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, using an Electric-type\nmove against a WOOPER (which is \na Water and Ground type) will end up\nhaving no effect due to its Ground type.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, if a Grass-type move (which\nis strong against both Water and\nGround types) is used, the damage\nwill be 4 times larger than usual.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The damage caused by a move is based\non type matchups and is decided by\nmultiplication.\nLet's say the Electric-type SHINX used\nthe Electric-type move Discharge against\nMANTYKE (a Water and Flying type).
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Pokémon's type and the move type are\nthe same, multiplying the damage by 1.5.\nElectric-type moves have an advantage\nover both Water and Flying types,\nmultiplying the damage by 4. With all these\nfactors, the damage is 6 times larger.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Furthermore, in the case of a critical hit,\nthe total damage is doubled. The move\nwill then cause 12 times larger than \nusual damage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Each move has a different effective range.\nCommonly, a move only affects one Pokémon.\nHowever, there are cases where moves \nhave the following effects:
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]・Effective against two opponents\n・Effective against all Pokémon but\n  the move's user, including Pokémon \n  in their own party \n・Effective against all Pokémon in\n  a battle
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves effective against two or more\nPokémon are very useful in Double Battles.\nHowever, the damage to each Pokémon\nbecomes smaller as the power is split up\namong targets.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When moves like Earthquake, Surf, \nor Discharge are used in Double Battle,\nyour teammate will also take damage.\nA little ingenuity is needed to use \nthese moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Some moves have added effects.\nIn addition to causing damage to \nopponents, some moves can change\nstats or cause status problems.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, Rock Smash has an\nadded effect that has a 50% chance to \nlower an opponent's Defense.\nThunder has an added effect that has a\n30% chance to paralyze an opponent.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]These moves are very useful in battle.\nThey not only damage the opponent,\nbut a similar effect to status moves \nis caused at the same time.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Normally, a Pokémon with the highest\nSpeed stat uses its move first.\nHowever, there are cases where the\norder of action is decided by a move\nand not by a Pokémon's Speed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, Quick Attack is a move that\nenables the user to strike first every time,\nregardless of Speed. On the contrary,\nVital Throw is a move that is sure to hit,\nbut always strikes last.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves that cause damage by directly\nstriking a foe's body are called \ndirect attacks. These direct attacks\ncan be physical moves or special moves.\n
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Direct attacks used against foes with\ncertain abilities, such as Poison Point or\nStatic, have a chance to afflict the \nattacker with various status problems.\nTry to use a move like Earthquake rather \nthan a direct attack against these foes.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Use moves to change weather.\nThese moves affect all Pokémon\nin battle. For example, Rain Dance is\na move that summons a heavy rain\nthat falls for five turns. During this time,\nWater-type moves are powered up.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Sunny Day intensifies the sun for five\nturns and powers up Fire-type moves \nduring its duration. Remember that it\npowers up not only your Pokémon's \nmoves, but also your foe's moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The move Hail causes hail to fall. \nAll Pokémon in battle will suffer damage\neach turn except for Ice-type Pokémon\nand Pokémon with the ability Snow Cloak. 
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Similarly, when Sandstorm is used,\nall Pokémon receive damage each turn\nexcept for Rock-, Steel-, or Ground-type \nPokémon and Pokémon that have the ability\nSand Veil.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are other moves that affect all the\nPokémon in a battle. For example,\nHaze is a move that eliminates \nall stat changes among all the \nPokémon engaged in battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, if Haze is used when you are\ntrying to raise your Pokémon's stats,\nall the effort will be for naught.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Also, moves such as Perish Song,\nGravity, and Trick Room affect all Pokémon\nin battle. Use these moves with deep\nconsideration.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]On the other hand, moves such as\nReflect, Light Screen, Safeguard, and\nMist only affect Pokémon on your team \nand not your opponent's.\nWhen you use moves, pay attention to\nthe effective range of those moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If Pokémon suffer from status problems\nsuch as sleep, paralysis, frozen, poison,\nburn, or confusion, they will take damage\nevery turn or will not be able to attack.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Have Pokémon hold Berries or use\nmoves to recover from status problems.\nA Lum Berry is especially useful, as it \ncan cure all status problems.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When a Pokémon is infatuated, there\nis a chance that the Pokémon won't attack.\nIn this case, the Pokémon will be cured\nif it is switched with another Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Two or more status problems like frozen,\nparalysis, poison, burn, or sleep won't\naffect a Pokémon at the same time.\nFor example, there will be no effect if a\nmove that makes a foe sleep is used\nagainst an opponent already poisoned.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, it is possible to confuse or\ninfatuate a Pokémon that already suffers\nfrom a status problem such as poison.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The effects caused by the following\nmoves can be added to status problems:\nNightmare, Encore, Torment, Whirlpool,\nDisable, Mean Look, Block, Ingrain, Curse,\nWrap, or Leech Seed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Status problems are mainly caused\nby moves. Other than that, some\nabilities of Pokémon may cause\nstatus problems too. 
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if an opponent's Pokémon\nhas the ability Synchronize and has a\nstatus problem such as poison, paralysis,\nor burn, the same status problem will affect\nyour Pokémon too.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are also abilities such as Static\nthat may cause paralysis to foes that\nuse direct attacks on the Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When it's hard to choose which\nPokémon to send out to battle, choose\nPokémon that have less disadvantaged\nmove-type matchups. For example,\nmany move types are not very effective \nagainst a Steel-type Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]But a Steel-type Pokémon has a \ndisadvantage against Fire-, Fighting-,\nand Ground-type moves.\nKeep Pokémon in your party that have\nadvantages against these move types.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Keeping this in mind, it is ideal to have a\nparty where each Pokémon can cover the\nweak points of the other Pokémon in the\nparty.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If you switch Pokémon, you'll take a\nfoe's attack at least one time.\nWhen choosing Pokémon to switch, \nchoose one that will take the least\npossible damage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if your foe has a Ground type\nand your Pokémon is an Electric type, \nyour foe will most likely use a Ground-type\nmove. Switch to a Flying-type Pokémon\nor one having the Levitate ability to be\nimmune to all Ground-type moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Additionally, if you switch in a Grass-type\nPokémon, the damage taken by Ground-type\nmoves will be reduced by half. Also, you can\ndeal the opponent a great amount of\ndamage by using Grass-type moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Having Pokémon learn moves to cover\nweaknesses is an effective strategy.\nFor example, if a Fighting-type Pokémon\nlearns Electric-, Dark-, Bug-, or Ice-type\nmoves, you can attack with super-\neffective moves to disadvantage foes.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]You don't have to switch your Pokémon\neither. Try a strategy of using Pokémon with\na high Speed stat to easily make the\nfirst attack.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When you choose moves in a battle,\nit is important to pay attention not \nonly to the type matchups, but also to your \nPokémon's stats.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]To utilize moves effectively, use \nphysical moves against an opponent's \nPokémon with low Defense, and\nuse special moves against an opponent's\nPokémon with low Special Defense.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, the Psychic-type ALAKAZAM\ndoesn't have a high Defense stat. You can\ncause huge damage using a high-powered\nphysical move like Earthquake without\nusing Dark-type moves that have an\nadvantageous matchup.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]You may wonder how you should utilize\nsome moves. There are moves with\nhigh power but low accuracy.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It may not be easy to fully utilize such\nmoves. However, if those moves are used\nin combination with other moves, items,\nor abilities, there is a chance to bring about\nunexpectedly great effects.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]These combinations are called combos\nin this game. You can check detailed\nexamples in the Advanced section of\nthe battle tutorials.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves that attack are categorized into\nphysical moves and special moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the past, physical moves and \nspecial moves depended on a\nmove's type. However, the way \nmoves are categorized has changed\nwith the DS Pokémon game.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Regardless of a move's type, whether\nit is a physical or special move depends\non the move itself.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the past, if more than one Pokémon were\nswitched in the same turn, the order of \naction was decided by the spots that the \nPokémon were standing in.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, the order of action is decided by\na Pokémon's Speed in the DS Pokémon game.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Speed decides not only the order of \nactions, but also the timing of effects\ntaking place, such as poison. The timing \nof when the next Pokémon appears after\na Pokémon has fainted has also changed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The next Pokémon will appear after all\nthe moves have been selected and \nused. It will never be attacked by a \nfoe before it has a chance to take action.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Some abilities take effect only while the \nPokémon is in battle. In the past,\nsuch abilities took effect immediately when\nthe Pokémon appeared. However, the timing\nof when abilities take effect has been \nchanged with the DS Pokémon game.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Such abilities take effect after all the\nPokémon appear in the battle. For example,\nafter two Pokémon appear in Single Battle \nor four Pokémon appear in a Double Battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the DS Pokémon game, a lot of new\nmoves are available. However, some\nmoves that existed in the past have\nhad their effects changed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, the effective range\nof Surf has been changed. In the past,\nSurf caused damage to only the\nopponent's Pokémon. However,\nit now affects all Pokémon but the \nuser.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Be careful. You may cause damage to the\nPokémon on your team in a Double Battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the DS Pokémon game, a lot of new\nspecial abilities were added. However,\nsome abilities that existed in the past\nhave had their effects changed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, the effect of Shadow Tag \nhas been changed. In the past, if you and\nyour opponent had a Pokémon with\nShadow Tag, neither side could switch\ntheir Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Now, Pokémon with the Shadow Tag\nability are unaffected by it, and can \nbe switched out normally.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Lightningrod will draw all Electric-type\nmoves not only from your foes but\nalso from the Pokémon on your team.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Stat-Changing Tactics
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Unexpected Effects of Critical Hits
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Item Tactics: 1
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Item Tactics: 2
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Special Ability Tactics
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Heal Block (Psychic Type)
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Psycho Shift (Psychic Type)

[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Moves Affecting All Pokémon + Special Abilities
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]Persim Berry + Swagger

[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 0][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Use status moves to raise your Pokémon's\nstats and lower the opponent's\nPokémon's stats in order to defeat strong\nPokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if a CLAYDOL, which\nnormally has a high Defense and\nSpecial Defense, uses Cosmic Power\nto raise these stats, it will not be\neasy to defeat that CLAYDOL.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]These moves that raise or lower stats\ncan be used over and over.\nTo avoid a foe's attack while using\nthese moves, raise your evasiveness first\nusing moves like Double Team or items\nlike BrightPowder.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The damage caused by critical hits\nis not influenced by any stat changes\nof your or your opponent's Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Critical hits always cause twice the\nnormal damage, even if a Pokémon's\nDefense or Sp. Defense has been raised.\nIn the same way, if your Pokémon's\nAttack or Sp. Attack are lowered, the\ndamage caused by them is not decreased.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Even if your opponent uses Reflect or\nLight Screen, the damage caused by\na critical hit is not decreased.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If you remember these things, your\ncritical hits will be more successful,\nand your win ratio for battles will increase.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Having Pokémon hold an item can\ncover weak points they may have.\nFor example, Rest is a move that\nfully restores the user's HP.\nBut there is the drawback that the user\ncan't make any actions for two turns.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If the user gets attacked by a foe while\nsleeping, the HP that has just been\nrestored will decrease.\nHave Pokémon hold a Chesto Berry to \nrecover from sleep right away, allowing\nthem to make an action on the next turn.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Some hold items can actually cause the\nholder to have a status problem or lowered\nstats. The move Fling enables the user to\nthrow an item at its opponent for its attack.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if an Iron Ball is thrown,\nit will cause massive damage to the\nopponent. If a Toxic Orb is thrown, it badly\npoisons the opponent.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Also, it can be rather interesting to\nexchange the item your Pokémon\nis holding with the one the opponent is\nholding using moves such as Trick or\nSwitcheroo.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If an Iron Ball is held by the opponent,\nit makes the Flying type, as well as\nlevitating holders, susceptible to\nGround moves as well as lowering\ntheir Speed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Not all special abilities have favorable\neffects. For example, SLAKING has the\nTruant ability; it can only attack once\nevery two turns.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, you can take advantage of\nabilities like this in Double Battles.\nSend out a Pokémon that has learned\nSkill Swap together with SLAKING to\nexchange abilities with SLAKING and\nthen with the foe in succeeding turns.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]SLAKING will be able to attack every\nturn, while the opponent will only be able\nto attack once every two turns, thus\nallowing you to kill two birds with one stone.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]As the name says, it prevents the foe\nfrom using any moves that recover HP.\nIf the opponent uses Recover or\nSoftboiled over and over, it gets hard to\ndefeat them, as they recover HP so quickly. \nUse this move if this is the case.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]This effect will continue for five turns.\nThough this is a Psychic-type move, it\nis effective against Dark-type Pokémon\nas well.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If used when paralyzed, poisoned,\nburned, or sleeping, the user can\ntransfer its status problem to its\ntarget.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, this always fails if the opponent\nalready has any status problems.\nIt is effective against Dark-type Pokémon\nas well.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It prevents the foe from using its held\nitem for five turns.\nMoves that utilize items, such as\nFling or Natural Gift, also can't be used.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It is effective against an opponent\nwho uses an item-and-move combo\nlike the Rest and Chesto Berry\ncombo described in "Advanced/\nAdvanced Battle Tips/Item Tactics: 1."
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The user draws its attack power by\nusing its held Berry; the Berry\ndetermines the move's type and power.\nFor example, using a held Cheri Berry has\nthe same effect as a Fire-type move\nwith 60 power.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Berries correspond to all types.\nSurprise your opponent by using\nmoves of the type that your Pokémon\ncan't normally learn.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, once the move is used, the\nBerry is gone.\nThis move will always fail if you aren't\nholding a Berry.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The more HP the foe has, the greater\nthis attack's power. On the other hand,\nif an opponent doesn't have much HP left,\nit is not very effective.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It is a very powerful move that,\nat its max, can have 120 power.\nUse it as soon as a battle begins to\nwring out an opponent's HP. It's a good\nidea to use other moves after that.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It makes Ground-type moves effective\nagainst Flying-type Pokémon, as well as\nPokémon that have the Levitate ability,\nfor five turns.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It also makes moves involving flying, \nsuch as Fly, Bounce, Splash,\nor Magnet Rise, unusable.\nIt also lowers the opponent's evasiveness.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If the opponent Pokémon is holding\na Berry, the user plucks it and gains\nits effect.\nIt is also effective when you don't \nwant your foe to use a Berry.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Bug-type move Bug Bite also has\nthe same effect.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Every time the opponent switches Pokémon,\nPoison Spikes poisons the one that comes\ninto battle. If it is used twice, the Pokémon\nwill be badly poisoned.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, it has no effect against Flying-\ntype Pokémon and Pokémon that\nhave the Levitate ability.\nAlso, it won't do anything against\nSteel-type Pokémon either.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If the opponent sends out a Poison-type\nPokémon, this move will have no effect,\nand Toxic Spikes also disappear.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A tricky move that enables slower Pokémon\nto get to move first for five turns.\nIt affects all of the Pokémon in the battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Its effect continues even after switching\nout the Pokémon. It may be a good idea to\nswitch in slower Pokémon after using\nthis move.\nIf the move is used again while it's already\nin effect, its effect will disappear.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]After making its attack, the user\nrushes back to switch places with\na waiting party Pokémon.\nUsually one turn is needed to switch\nPokémon, and no attack can be made\nin that turn.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, this move enables the user to\nattack and switch in the same turn.\nAs it's effective when used as the first\nattack, have high-Speed Pokémon\nlearn this move and switch with the\nPokémon that have better matchups.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]An attack that only hits a foe using\nProtect or Detect. It also removes the\neffects of both of those moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In a Double Battle, it's an effective\ntactic to remove the effects of Protect\nor Detect first, then use powerful moves\nto attack.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]As the name states, the user flings its\nheld item at the foe to attack. \nThe item flung will disappear.\nIts power and effect depend on\nthe item.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if the item thrown is\na King's Rock, it may cause the foe to flinch\nwhen damage is inflicted.\nAlso, some Berries have effects that\nraise a Pokémon's stats when flung.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In a Double Battle, it's an effective\ntactic to fling Berries.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]This is the perfect move to eliminate the\neffect of an opponent's ability.\nIt's very useful when opponent\nPokémon have favorable abilities\nagainst your Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Worry Seed has a similar effect, but its\neffect is that it changes the opponent's\nability to Insomnia, thus preventing\nthe opponent from going to sleep.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, remember that Worry Seed has\nno effect against SLAKING, who has the\nTruant ability.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It reduces the opponent's evasion stat\nby one, and also eliminates the effects of\nmoves such as Light Screen, Reflect,\nSafeguard, or Mist.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, when your Pokémon has\nalready used Spikes, Toxic Spikes,\nor Stealth Rock, their effects will also\nbe removed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A Pokémon with this ability can attack\nwithout suffering the negatives of a\ntype disadvantage. For example, if the\ndamage is supposed to be halved because\nthe move is "not very effective," it will\nstill cause the full amount of damage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the same way, if the move is "not very\neffective," and the damage is supposed\nto be one-fourth of normal, it will only be\nhalf of normal instead.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves can be used regardless of the\nopponent's abilities. For example,\nGround-type moves can't hit a Pokémon that\nhas Levitate as its ability. However,\nMold Breaker makes it possible.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, there is no effect against abilities\nthat take effect after an attack (such as\nRough Skin or Static). Be careful,\na direct attack against a Pokémon with the\nRough Skin ability still inflicts the usual\namount of damage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Normally, if a move becomes a critical hit,\nit can inflict twice the amount of normal\ndamage. However, this ability increases the\namount of damage dealt when a critical hit\nis landed.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If a Pokémon with this ability learns a\nmove or has a hold item that raises\nthe chance of it getting a critical hit,\nit will be a huge threat to your opponent.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It powers up moves that are power 60\nor less to 1.5 times their normal power.\nYou'll see a greater effect when using\nmoves like Fury Swipes that hit multiple\ntimes.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When moves that change their own\npower--such as Frustration--are used,\nthe effect will still take place as long as\nits power turns out to be 60 or less.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Only ELECTIVIRE has this ability.\nNot only does it prevent damage from\nElectric-type moves, but it also increases\nthe Pokémon's Speed stat by one.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if you send out a Water-\nor Flying-type Pokémon and\nthe opponent tries to use any Electric-type\nmoves, switch to a Pokémon with this ability.\nYou'll be sure to have the advantage.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It decreases the damage when hit by\na supereffective move.\nOnly MIME JR. and MR. MIME (both Psychic\ntype) can have this ability.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In fact, a Pokémon with this ability becomes\nstrong against Ghost- or Dark-type moves\nthat are unfavorable matchups against\nthem. The ability Solid Rock also has a\nsimilar effect.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]CAMERUPT or RHYPERIOR can have\nthis ability. If a Pokémon is resilient to\ndamage, even if attacked by an opponent\nwith a favorable type matchup (like a Water\nor Ground type), they are likely to\nhave this ability.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]BUNEARY and LOPUNNY can have this\nability. They can't use any held items during\nthe battle.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It may be ambiguous as to how this ability\nis useful, but it's a good idea to have them\nhold an item that causes status problems\nor lowers their stats.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Utilize this ability together with\nthe move Switcheroo to trade held\nitems with your opponent.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When a Pokémon with this ability gets KO'd\nby a direct-attack move, it causes an\nexplosion and inflicts damage equal to\none-fourth of the attacking Pokémon's\nmax HP. DRIFLOON, DRIFBLIM, STUNKY,\nand SKUNTANK can have this ability.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When fighting a Pokémon with this ability,\nuse moves that aren't direct attacks so that\nyour Pokémon won't take any damage when\nyou do knock the opponent out.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The Choice Band boosts Attack by 1.5.\nChoice Specs boosts Sp. Attack by 1.5.\nHowever, these items allow the use of only\none kind of move.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Choose which item your Pokémon will hold\nwhile carefully considering the Pokémon's\nstats and moves.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Use Rain Dance to make it rain, then follow\nit up by using Thunder.\nNormally the accuracy of Thunder is\n70; however, when it's raining it's sure\nto hit the opponent.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In the same way, use Blizzard when it's\nhailing so that the move will never fail\nto hit the opponent.\nAnother staple weather combo is\nSunny Day and SolarBeam.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It normally takes two turns to use\nSolarBeam. But if the weather is clear and\nsunny, it can be used in one turn.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Toxic is a move that leaves the target\nbadly poisoned. As the damage caused\nby the poison worsens every turn,\nthe opponent will likely try to switch\nout Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, if a move like Mean Look (which\nkeeps your opponent from switching\nPokémon) is used beforehand, it is very\nlikely that you will easily defeat them.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]A similar tactic is the Wrap and Leech\nSeed combo. Wrap not only keeps the foe\nfrom fleeing, but also inflicts damage on the\nfoe for two to five turns.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In addition, Leech Seed steals some HP\nfrom the foe every turn.\nThere's no doubt your opponent will be\ntroubled by your tactics.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]When Endure is used, the user is able to\nbarely endure any strong attack and be left\nwith 1 HP. Use Reversal after that.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Reversal is a move that becomes more\npowerful the less HP the user has.\nThis is an opportunity to inflict huge\ndamage to your opponent.\nHowever, unless you can attack first\nin the next turn, you'll be defeated.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Be sure to paralyze your opponent and\nlower its Speed beforehand.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Sniper is an ability that powers up\nmoves by increasing the damage they\ncause if they become critical hits.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Have Pokémon with this ability hold\na Scope Lens or Razor Claw to boost their\ncritical-hit ratio.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]In addition, have it learn moves like Night\nSlash or Slash, which have a high\ncritical-hit ratio. By doing this, you can\ntake full advantage of Sniper's effect.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]This tactic is effective for Pokémon that\nhave the ability Super Luck, too.\nUtilizing both moves and items, try to get\nthose critical hits.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Facade is a move that doubles in power\nif the user is poisoned, paralyzed,\nor burned. However, in battle, the opponent\nmay not always use moves that cause\nstatus problems.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]So, it's best to give your Pokémon status\nproblems deliberately by having it hold\na Toxic Orb or Flame Orb. However, these\norbs don't take effect until the end of the\nturn that the Pokémon holding them\nappeared.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Use moves like Protect while you wait for\nthe item to take effect, then use Facade.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Pokémon that work best with this tactic are\nones that have the ability Guts.\nGuts boosts Attack by 1.5 if they have\na status problem, so the damage they inflict\non the opponent will be even larger.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]If you have a Pokémon that has learned\nBaton Pass, it's worthwhile to try this.\nWhen Baton Pass is used, the user switches\nplaces with the next Pokémon, passing\nalong any stat changes caused by\nstatus moves.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Use Swords Dance or Double Team\nfirst to raise their Attack or evasiveness.\nThen, transfer the effect to the next\nPokémon so that it can battle under\nfavorable conditions from the beginning.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]As Baton Pass can transfer multiple stat\nchanges, it's also effective to use both\nDouble Team and Swords Dance.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Also, Pokémon that have Speed-boosting\nabilities (like NINJASK) can pass along the\nraised Speed stat with this ability.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Moves like Earthquake, Surf, or Lava Plume\nare very handy in a Double Battle, as the\nmoves can attack both of the foe's Pokémon\nat the same time. However, these moves also\nhit your Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Because of this, have your Pokémon learn\nmoves such as Protect or Detect.\nEither move can be used first, regardless\nof the Pokémon's Speed. That way, it can\nprevent damage.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It is also a wise tactic to utilize abilities\nto prevent your Pokémon from taking any\ndamage by moves like Earthquake, which\ncan hurt ally Pokémon.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]For example, if you want to use Earthquake,\nsend out a Flying-type ally Pokémon, or one\nthat has the Levitate ability, to avoid being\ndamaged by the attack.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There will be no need for the Pokémon\nto use moves like Protect or Detect, so\nthey will be able to attack as well.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Also, be sure to remember the\nfollowing combos:\n \nSurf + ability: Water Absorb\nDischarge + ability: Volt Absorb\nLava Plume + ability: Flash Fire
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]These combos can restore ally Pokémon\nor raise a move's power as well as\nprevent them from taking damage.\nMake good use of these combos to\nbattle advantageously.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Swagger is a move that raises the foe's\nAttack stat by 2 and confuses it.\nAlthough it's usually used on a foe to\nlead them to self-destructing, use\nthe move on a Pokémon on your side.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The key is to have your ally Pokémon hold\na Persim Berry. Since the Persim Berry will\ncure confusion, only the Attack stat will\nbe raised.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]The move Flatter, which raises the target's\nSp. Attack stat and confuses them, can\ntake the place of Swagger in this combo.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]It's also a good idea to send out Pokémon\nthat have the Own Tempo ability or to use\nSafeguard, which prevents status problems,\ninstead of having Pokémon hold\na Persim Berry.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Simple is an ability that causes the Pokémon\nwith it to be more influenced by stat \nchanges than normal.\nOf course, it works well with moves that\nraise stats, but how about an unusual\ncombo with Acupressure?
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Acupressure boosts either Attack, Defense,\nSp. Attack, Sp. Defense, Speed, accuracy,\nor evasiveness by 2 levels.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]There are no Pokémon with the Simple ability\nthat can learn Acupressure; however,\nin a Double Battle, ally Pokémon can use it.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]You'll never know which stat will rise\nuntil it is actually used.\nBut it can sharply boost a stat.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]This move eliminates the effects of\nabilities. For example, REGIGIGAS has the\nability Slow Start, which is rather annoying\nsince it halves Attack and Speed for\nfive turns.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]However, if its ally uses Gastro Acid,\nit can fight at full power, starting on the\nfirst turn.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Psych Up is a move that copies other\nPokémon's stat changes to the user.\nWhile one Pokémon uses Belly Drum to raise\nits Attack, the ally Pokémon uses Psych Up\nto copy the stat changes.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]By doing this, both Pokémon can sharply\nboost the power of their physical moves.\nIn the same way, copying the effect of\nFocus Energy is also recommended.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1]Doing so will raise the critical-hit ratio of\nboth Pokémon, creating a massive threat\nfor your opponent.

[FONT 1][SPACING 1][COLOR 3]How to use the Pokémon Wheel.\n[COLOR 5]In a Fortune Battle, your Pokémon\nand your opponent's will be mixed.\nThe Pokémon that will enter the\nbattle are chosen by the wheel.\n[COLOR 1]Hold the Wii Remote vertically.
[FONT 1][SPACING 1][COLOR 3]1. How to hold the Wii Remote.\n[COLOR 5]Hold the Wii Remote vertically.\nThen, point it at the wheel.\nIf you chose to use the Sideways\ncontrols, you'll need to hold\nthe remote vertically here.\c
[FONT 1][SPACING 1][COLOR 3]2. Placement of Pokémon.\n[COLOR 5]Both your Pokémon and your\nopponent's are placed on\nthe wheel.\nThe background color shows the\nPokémon's Type.\c
[FONT 1][SPACING 1][COLOR 3]3. Spinning the wheel.\n[COLOR 5]Point at the START button at the\ncenter of the wheel and press the\nA Button to spin the wheel.\c
[FONT 1][SPACING 1][COLOR 3]4. Choose a Pokémon.\n[COLOR 5]Point the Wii Remote at any\nspot on the wheel and press the\nA Button.\nA Poké Ball will fall onto the wheel,\nand a Pokémon will be chosen.\c
[FONT 1][SPACING 1][COLOR 3]5. Starting the battle.\n[COLOR 5]You and your opponent will\ntake turns choosing Pokémon.\nChoose three Pokémon for Single\nBattle and four for Double Battle.\nThe battle will then begin![VAR 0067]
